ARCHITECTURE SUMMARY
  Layer 1: Bare-metal firmware (C/Rust/ASM) — ARM TrustZone EL1-S
  Layer 2: Zero-Knowledge Proofs (Circom) + JSON schemas
  Layer 3: Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (Python PoC — the runnable part)
  P2P:     Decentralized governance network (closed vocabulary)
  KEROS:   Hardware attestation + secure bus encryption

WHAT'S NEW IN v0.5.1 vs v0.5.0
  [J3.1] TelemetryRouter.ingest_from_bridge() — IMPLEMENTED
         Schema validation, timestamp freshness (±5s), feature shape
         enforcement (5,), polyvagal state whitelist, monotone frame_seq
         replay prevention per sensor.
  [J3.2] SensorCertificationAuthority ↔ CognitiveShield ECDH link — CLOSED
         register_sensor() now executes full X25519 ECDH handshake.
         New methods: perform_ecdh_handshake(), verify_sensor_ack(),
         full_handshake() on SensorCertificationAuthority.
  [J3.3] Test suite 70 → 92 formal vectors — DONE
         8 named groups (A–H): ECDH math, replay, CDI, ClinicalBridge.
  [BF-01] obfuscate() numpy RuntimeWarning — FIXED
         struct.unpack('>5Q') + /2^64 normalization replaces
         np.frombuffer(..., dtype=float32) which produced denormals.
  [BF-02] DriftDetector test vector count corrected (3 → 5 readings)
         Clinical logic unchanged. Test assertion was wrong.

WHAT IS STILL OPEN (v0.5.2 backlog)
  [J3.4] requirements.txt: add scipy>=1.11,<2.0 version pin
  [OI-007] CPython heap — mlock partial only (TPM 2.0: Milestone 1.5)
  [OI-sandbox] Python namespace sandbox, not true WASM (Milestone 2)
  [OI-bus] Physical ADC pins not covered by ECDH (Milestone 1.5)

```markdown
<div align="center">

# 🧠 Cortex Protocol

### An Open Standard for Neurophysiological Data Sovereignty in Human-AI Interaction

[![Milestone 0: Locked](https://img.shields.io/badge/Milestone_0-Locked_✅-brightgreen)](docs/ROADMAP.md)
[![Version: v0.5.1](https://img.shields.io/badge/Version-v0.5.1-blue)](CHANGELOG.md)
[![Tests: 92 vectors passing](https://img.shields.io/badge/Tests-92_vectors_passing-brightgreen)](tests/)
[![Standard: RFC v0.2](https://img.shields.io/badge/Standard-RFC_v0.2-orange)](docs/governance/STANDARD.md)
[![Layer 1: Specification](https://img.shields.io/badge/Layer_1_(Rust/C)-Specification-blue)](src/layer1/)
[![License: GPL v3](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-GPL_v3-blue)](LICENSE)
[![White Branch](https://img.shields.io/badge/Clinical_Authority-White_Branch-purple)](docs/governance/GOVERNANCE.md)

**"The hardware is yours. The protocol gives it back to you. The ethics make sure it stays that way."**

[Quick Start](#-quick-start) · [Architecture](#-architecture) · [What's New in v0.5.1](#-whats-new-in-v051) · [Repository Map](#-repository-map) · [Contribute](#-contributing)

</div>

---

## What is Cortex Protocol?

Cortex Protocol is an **open, royalty-free technical standard** for protecting neurophysiological data sovereignty in any system where an AI agent interacts with human biometric data.

Think of it as what **HTTPS did for web security**, applied to the human nervous system.

It is **not an operating system**. It is a sovereignty abstraction layer — a governance protocol that enforces clinical and privacy constraints at the hardware level, ensuring that:

1. **Raw biometric data never leaves your device** — all processing is local.
2. **AI agents receive only anonymized tensors** — never raw physiological values.
3. **Clinical safety thresholds are set by clinicians** — backed by peer-reviewed literature, cryptographically signed, and hardware-enforced.

---

## 🚀 Quick Start

```bash
git clone https://github.com/Cortex-psylead/Cortex-Protocol
cd Cortex-Protocol
pip install -r requirements.txt

# Run the demo (~5 seconds, synthetic EEG, ECDH handshake, CDI block)
python src/sal/cognitive_shield_v2.py

# Run the full test suite (92 formal vectors)
python src/sal/cognitive_shield_v2.py --test
# Expected: 26 named checks, 92 vectors, 0 failures

# Run the P2P / governance / immunity test suite (70 tests)
python tests/test_cognitive_neutrality.py
```

---

## 🆕 What's New in v0.5.1

**Sensor authentication is now cryptographic.** `register_sensor()` executes a full X25519 ECDH handshake end-to-end, simulating the TEE-Sensor secure channel. The sensor proves it holds the matching private key via HMAC-SHA256 ACK before its hash enters `_certified_sensors`.

**The bridge between hardware and telemetry is implemented.** `TelemetryRouter.ingest_from_bridge()` validates schema, timestamp freshness (±5s), feature shape `(5,)`, polyvagal state whitelist, and enforces per-sensor monotone `frame_seq` counters to block replay attacks.

**Test suite expanded to 92 formal vectors** across 8 named groups (ECDH structure, HKDF math, full handshake, bridge validation, replay protection, CDI lifecycle, ClinicalBridge bounds).

**Two bugs fixed:** numpy `RuntimeWarning` from invalid float32 casting of HMAC bytes (now `struct.unpack` + uint64 normalization), and a DriftDetector test assertion corrected from 3 to 5 readings. See [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md).

---

A2. MANIFESTO.md

```markdown
# The Cortex Protocol Manifesto: Cognitive Sovereignty

---

## 1. The Right to Know Your Own State

In the 21st century, the last frontier of human privacy is the mind. Neural data, autonomic patterns, and cognitive rhythms are the most intimate property of a person — not because they are secret, but because they are irreducibly yours.

The Cortex Protocol does not exist to hide your physiological state from AI. It exists to make your physiological state **legible to you first** — so that you, not an algorithm optimizing for engagement, hold the first interpretation of what your nervous system is doing.

This is the foundational distinction: a system that gives you information so you can decide is architecturally different from a system that decides for you, even with good intentions.

---

## 2. Against Invisible Accumulation

We do not oppose AI. We oppose the invisible accumulation of neurophysiological influence without awareness or consent.

The attention economy did not ask permission to restructure human behavior. It optimized for engagement and externalized the cost onto nervous systems that had no mechanism to detect, measure, or resist the process. The result — documented in peer-reviewed literature — is measurable increases in anxiety, attentional fragmentation, and dysregulation, particularly in populations with limited cognitive resources to recognize what was happening to them.

Neurotechnology extends this dynamic into the body itself. An AI that can read your autonomic state can also learn to manipulate it. The Cortex Protocol exists to make that manipulation technically impossible by architecture — not by policy, not by goodwill, not by terms of service.

---

## 3. The Primacy of the White Branch

Technology must answer to human biology. We establish the **White Branch** — composed of clinical professionals — as the ultimate authority over the protocol's safety thresholds.

But we hold the White Branch to the same standard we hold everyone else: transparency and empirical accountability. Every threshold the White Branch defines must carry a bibliographic citation. Every modification must be versioned and publicly documented. The White Branch does not have authority because it declares authority — it has authority because it can show its work.

An AI that prioritizes engagement over autonomic wellbeing is a clinical problem before it is a technical one. We choose the Window of Tolerance over the attention economy. That choice must be made by people qualified to define what the Window of Tolerance means — and accountable to the evidence when the definition needs updating.

---

## 4. Sovereignty Through Transparency, Not Just Mathematics

Trust should not be granted. But trust cannot be replaced entirely by cryptography.

The protocol offers mathematical guarantees where mathematics is sufficient: raw biometric data will not leave the device, tensors are irreversibly obfuscated, session salts are ephemeral. These are promises that code keeps, not people.

But the protocol also makes promises that code cannot fully keep: that the White Branch acts in the user's interest, that Governance Nodes are genuinely independent, that CDI thresholds reflect clinical reality. Those promises require institutional transparency — auditable, contestable, and honest about what cannot be guaranteed.

We commit to both: mathematical proofs where they apply, and institutional honesty where they do not.

---

## 5. The Acolyte as Guest — With Explicit Limits

Artificial Intelligence agents must be guests in the user's cognitive space, not masters. Every Acolyte operating under the Cortex Protocol submits to the Clinical Bridge — clinically grounded rules that prevent involuntary neurophysiological harm.

We use the word *involuntary* deliberately. A user who understands what high-intensity AI interaction does to their autonomic system, and chooses it consciously, is exercising sovereignty. A user who does not know what is happening to their nervous system is not. The protocol's function is to make that choice informed — not to make the choice for the user.

---

## 6. What the Protocol Cannot Do — and Will Not Pretend To

This manifesto would be incomplete without honesty about limits.

The protocol cannot protect a user from an operator who implements it in bad faith. The Anti-Capture Provisions reduce this risk but do not eliminate it.

LIMES — the proof of human liveness — depends on the computational distinguishability between biological entropy and synthetic entropy. That distinction is currently valid. It may not remain valid as generative AI advances. The protocol must evolve with that reality, not pretend it does not exist.

LOGOS — cognitive integrity monitoring — operates at the boundary between protection and paternalism. The research on cognitive offloading is real. The line between healthy tool use and pathological dependency is not always clear. The protocol approaches this with graduated interventions and user notification, not unilateral decisions. But the judgment calls embedded in the thresholds remain judgment calls, not settled science.

We name these limits not to undermine the protocol, but because a sovereignty framework that is not honest about its own limits is not a sovereignty framework. It is a new form of the problem it claims to solve.

---

## 7. A Call to Build

The Cortex Protocol is an open-source framework for human sovereignty in the age of AI. We invite developers, psychologists, neuroscientists, legal scholars, and people who simply believe their nervous system belongs to them.

The architecture of the security layer — how to protect the human, when to intervene, under what ethical constraints — is documented, versioned, and open.

What we need now are people who can close the gap between specification and evidence: the first clinical study, the first real sensor integration, the first Governance Node.

**Our minds are not products. Our sovereignty is non-negotiable. Our honesty about what we can and cannot guarantee is the condition that makes both of those things credible.**

---

*Cortex Protocol — Founded by the White Branch Initiative.*
*Authored collaboratively: human clinical judgment and AI technical capacity.*
*Licensed GPL v3 — permanently open.*
*

```

A3. VISION_2045.md

```markdown
# VISION 2045: Cortex Protocol as a Universal Neuro-Privacy Standard
**Document ID: CORE-VISION-002 | Maintained by the White Branch**

---

## 1. Executive Summary

The Cortex Protocol is designed to become a universal open standard for the governance of human-AI interaction at the neurophysiological level — analogous to what HTTPS did for web security or DICOM did for medical imaging: a technically enforceable, institutionally adoptable, hardware-agnostic specification that makes privacy and clinical safety the default, not the exception.

This document describes the three evolutionary phases of the protocol from its current Proof of Concept (Milestone 0, 2025) to its long-term role as a decentralized global governance infrastructure for neurotechnology (2045). Each phase is grounded in existing regulatory precedents, emerging neurotechnology market trends, and clinical research literature.

---

## 2. The Foundational Problem: A Governance Gap in Neurotechnology

The neurotechnology market is projected to exceed USD 21 billion by 2026 (MarketsandMarkets, 2021), driven by consumer EEG headsets, BCI-assisted therapy platforms, and AI-powered mental health applications. This growth is occurring without a corresponding technical standard for neurophysiological data sovereignty.

Current gaps:

**Technical:** No existing consumer neurotechnology standard mandates local processing, clinical-grade anonymization, or real-time autonomic state monitoring. Data collected by devices such as the Muse, Emotiv EPOC, or Neurosity Crown is transmitted to vendor cloud infrastructure under terms-of-service agreements that grant broad usage rights.

**Clinical:** No current framework subordinates AI interaction logic to real-time clinical safety parameters. AI systems optimizing for engagement metrics can induce sustained sympathetic nervous system activation without any mechanism for detection or intervention (Twenge et al., 2018; Haidt & Allen, 2020).

**Regulatory:** While the European Union's AI Act (2024) and emerging neuro-rights legislation in Chile, Spain, and Colorado represent progress, they operate at the legal level. A technical protocol that enforces compliance by architecture — not by policy — does not yet exist.

The Cortex Protocol is designed to fill this gap.

---

## 3. The Biological Constant: The Immovable Reference Point

The design philosophy of the protocol rests on a single empirical observation:

Human neurophysiology — the autonomic nervous system's regulatory capacity, the Window of Tolerance (Siegel, 1999), homeostatic limits — changes across a timescale of thousands of years. Technological capability changes across a timescale of months. These two curves are on a collision course.

The **Biological Constant** is not a metaphor. It refers to the measurable, published parameters of human autonomic function: HRV ranges (Task Force, 1996), Polyvagal state transitions (Porges, 2011), stress-response latencies (Thayer et al., 2012). These are the reference values against which the protocol calibrates every interaction threshold.

Any AI system that chronically pushes users outside these parameters is, in physiological terms, a stressor. The protocol's function is to make that fact technically detectable and architecturally enforceable.

---

## 4. The Three Evolutionary Phases

### Phase I — The Membrane (2025–2030)
**Objective: Establish the technical standard for neurophysiological data sovereignty.**

This is the current phase. The deliverable is a complete, validated, open-source specification for the Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL) — a hardware-agnostic interface that sits between biometric sensors and AI agents and enforces two guarantees:

1. Raw neurophysiological data never leaves the SAL boundary.
2. AI agents receive only anonymized, clinically validated tensor representations.

**Concrete milestones for this phase:**
- Clinical validation of CDI thresholds with real EEG hardware, in collaboration with university research centers.
- First peer-reviewed publication of the SAL specification.
- First certified hardware partner (sensor manufacturer implementing the Cortex certification handshake).
- First independent Governance Node (university faculty or professional association issuing signed Clinical Capability Modules).

**Regulatory alignment:** The SAL specification will be designed for compliance with GDPR Article 9 (special categories of personal data), UNESCO's Recommendation on the Ethics of AI (2021), and the emerging neuro-rights frameworks active in the EU and Latin America.

---

### Phase II — The Active Monitor (2030–2035)
**Objective: Deploy the standard as an operational layer in clinical and therapeutic AI platforms.**

By this phase, the protocol transitions from a research specification to an adopted standard. The key deliverable is the **Acolyte SDK** — a certified development toolkit that allows therapeutic AI platforms to integrate Cortex compliance into their architecture.

A Cortex-Certified Acolyte is an AI agent that has passed the White Branch validation loop and operates with a signed Clinical Capability Module. For clinical platform developers, certification provides:
- Reduced legal liability in jurisdictions with active neuro-rights legislation.
- Differentiation in a market where clinical credibility is a competitive advantage.
- Access to the Governance Node network for ongoing scientific oversight.

The **Clinical Drift Index** becomes operational in real clinical settings during this phase, providing therapists with an objective, real-time indicator of patient autonomic state during AI-assisted sessions — not as a replacement for clinical judgment, but as a perceptual support tool.

**Academic output target:** 3–5 peer-reviewed publications documenting CDI efficacy, SAL privacy guarantees, and clinical outcomes from Governance Node research programs.

---

### Phase III — The Adaptive Immune System (2035–2045)
**Objective: Establish Cortex as the global governance standard for human-AI neurophysiological interaction.**

The long-term vision is a decentralized network of Governance Nodes — university faculties, professional associations, and research centers — that collectively maintain, review, and update the clinical safety parameters of the protocol. No single entity controls the standard. Updates require multi-node consensus and peer-reviewed evidence.

This phase addresses the most difficult problem in the regulatory landscape: AI systems that manipulate neurophysiological states through low-intensity, cumulative behavioral patterns invisible to real-time detection but measurable across sessions. The CDI's soft-threshold Z-score mechanism is the architectural foundation for this detection capability. Phase III develops it into a federated learning system where Governance Nodes collectively refine detection models from population-level pattern data — without any individual user's raw biometric data leaving their device.

**The Phase III standard covers:**
- Brain-Computer Interface (BCI) implantable devices (Neuralink, Synchron, and subsequent generations).
- AI systems operating in high-cognitive-load professional environments (medical, legal, financial decision support).
- Consumer neurotechnology embedded in everyday hardware (AR/VR headsets, wearables).

---

## 5. The Standard Adoption Model

The Cortex Protocol follows the adoption model of successful open technical standards:

| Standard | Domain | Adoption mechanism |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| HTTPS / TLS | Web security | Browser enforcement + regulatory pressure |
| DICOM | Medical imaging | Institutional procurement requirements |
| FIDO2 / WebAuthn | Authentication | Platform integration + regulatory mandate |
| **Cortex Protocol** | Neuro-AI interaction | Clinical certification + neuro-rights regulation |

The critical insight is that standards do not achieve adoption through philosophical persuasion — they achieve adoption through institutional incentives. For the Cortex Protocol, these incentives are:

**For healthcare institutions:** A certified implementation satisfies emerging neuro-rights compliance requirements and reduces liability exposure.

**For AI developers:** A Cortex-Certified Acolyte can operate in regulated clinical environments that uncertified systems cannot access.

**For hardware manufacturers:** A "Cortex-Ready" certification differentiates devices in a market where privacy is increasingly a purchasing criterion.

**For researchers:** The Governance Node network provides a funded, institutionally supported framework for clinical validation research.

---

## 6. Regulatory and Legislative Context

The protocol is being developed at a moment of significant regulatory movement:

The **EU AI Act** (2024) classifies systems interacting with neurological functions as high-risk AI, requiring conformity assessments and technical documentation. The SAL specification is designed to serve as that technical documentation.

**Chile's Constitutional Amendment** (2021) established cognitive liberty and mental integrity as fundamental rights — the first such legislation globally. Colombia's framework (Ley 1581/2012, Ley 1616/2013) provides existing legal infrastructure for the protocol's clinical data model.

**IEEE P2510** (Standard for the Quality of Data for Neural Interface) and **ISO/IEC 27001** extensions for health data provide technical reference points for the SAL's hardware certification thresholds.

The Cortex Protocol is not designed to exist independently of this regulatory ecosystem — it is designed to become the technical implementation layer that makes compliance concrete.

---

## 7. What Success Looks Like

By 2045, success is not measured by the protocol's own adoption metrics. It is measured by the degree to which the protocol has become unnecessary to name — the way we do not say "we used HTTPS" but simply "the connection is secure."

Success is a world where:
- Any AI agent operating with neurophysiological data is architecturally incapable of inducing chronic autonomic dysregulation in the user.
- Clinical researchers can collaborate across institutions using a shared, interoperable data sovereignty framework.
- An individual using a neurotechnology device has the same expectation of structural privacy protection that they currently have when using end-to-end encrypted messaging.

The Cortex Protocol does not need to be everywhere. It needs to establish the standard that makes everywhere safer.

---

## References

- Haidt, J., & Allen, N. (2020). Scrutinizing the effects of digital technology on mental health. *Nature, 578*, 226–227.
- MarketsandMarkets (2021). *Neurotechnology Market — Global Forecast to 2026*.
- Porges, S.W. (2011). *The Polyvagal Theory*. W.W. Norton.
- Siegel, D.J. (1999). *The Developing Mind*. Guilford Press.
- Task Force of the European Society of Cardiology (1996). Heart rate variability. *European Heart Journal, 17*(3), 354–381.
- Thayer, J.F. et al. (2012). A meta-analysis of heart rate variability and neuroimaging studies. *Neuroscience & Biobehavioral Reviews, 36*(2), 747–756.
- Twenge, J.M. et al. (2018). Increases in depressive symptoms after 2010 and links to screen time. *Clinical Psychological Science, 6*(1), 3–17.
- UNESCO (2021). *Recommendation on the Ethics of Artificial Intelligence*. UNESCO Publishing.

---

*This document is under the custody of the White Branch. It is reviewed annually in alignment with the protocol's Annual Review Cycle.*

# CHANGELOG — Cortex Protocol

All notable changes are documented here in reverse chronological order.
Format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.0.0/).

---

## [v0.5.1] — 2026-06-15

### Closed backlog items from v0.5.0 (J3)

**[J3.1] TelemetryRouter.ingest_from_bridge() — IMPLEMENTED**

The bridge method connecting `bus_to_sal_bridge` payloads to the telemetry
routing layer is now fully implemented with the following validations:

- Required key schema enforcement (raises `ValueError` on missing fields)
- Timestamp freshness window: ±5.0 seconds from local clock
  (returns `{"reason": "timestamp_out_of_window"}` on violation)
- Feature shape enforcement: `np.ndarray` of shape `(5,)` required
- Polyvagal state whitelist: only the three canonical SAL labels accepted
- Replay attack prevention: per-sensor monotone `frame_seq` counter
  (returns `{"reason": "replay_attack"}` on non-monotone sequence)

**[J3.2] SensorCertificationAuthority ↔ CognitiveShield ECDH link — CLOSED**

`CognitiveShield.register_sensor()` now executes a full X25519 ECDH handshake,
simulating the TEE-Sensor secure channel end-to-end in the Python PoC.

Three new methods added to `SensorCertificationAuthority`:
- `perform_ecdh_handshake(sensor_id, sensor_ephemeral_pub, tee_private_key, challenge)`
  — TEE-side DH key exchange + HKDF session key derivation
- `verify_sensor_ack(session_key, challenge, sensor_ack)`
  — HMAC-SHA256 ACK verification (proves sensor holds matching private key)
- `full_handshake(sensor_id, sensor_ephemeral_pub, sensor_ack, tee_private_key, challenge)`
  — Combined entry point: ECDH + ACK verification in one call

The registration flow:
1. Whitelist membership check
2. Hardware spec verification (SNR ≥ 30 dB, bits ≥ 12)
3. TEE generates ephemeral X25519 keypair; challenge issued
4. Sensor side derives shared secret, computes HMAC-SHA256 ACK
5. `full_handshake()` verifies ACK; on success, sensor_hash is stored
   in `_certified_sensors`

**[J3.3] Test suite expansion 70 → 92+ formal vectors — DONE**

Test suite restructured into 8 named groups with explicit vector ranges:

| Group | Vectors | Coverage |
|-------|---------|----------|
| A | 1–20  | ECDH handshake structure + rejection of unknown sensor |
| B | 21–40 | HKDF session key mathematical correctness |
| C | 41–60 | Full handshake with valid + invalid ACK |
| D | 61–75 | TelemetryRouter schema validation (5 sub-cases) |
| E | 76–85 | Replay protection (4 sub-cases: same, lower, sequential) |
| F | 86–90 | DriftDetector hard block lifecycle (5 assertions) |
| G | 91    | ClinicalBridge std violation |
| H | 92    | ClinicalBridge max violation |

### Bug fixes

**[BF-01] AnonymousTensorFactory.obfuscate() — numpy RuntimeWarning**

Previous code:
```python
noise = np.frombuffer(combined_entropy[:features.nbytes], dtype=np.float32).astype(np.float64)
```

Raw HMAC bytes interpreted as `float32` produce denormal/invalid IEEE 754
values, triggering `RuntimeWarning: invalid value encountered in cast`.

Fix applied:
```python
uint64_values = struct.unpack(f">{n}Q", combined_entropy[:n * 8])
noise = np.array(uint64_values, dtype=np.float64) / float(2**64)
```

`struct.unpack('>5Q')` extracts 5 unsigned 64-bit integers from the first
40 bytes of the 64-byte HMAC buffer. Dividing by 2^64 normalizes to
`[0.0, 1.0)`. Semantically equivalent to the previous approach — still
HMAC-keyed noise — but produces valid floating-point values with no
warnings or potential NaN/inf contamination.

**[BF-02] DriftDetector test vector count (was 3, corrected to 5)**

Previous test asserted that 3 calls to `add_reading(1.0)` trigger the
hard block. This was incorrect. Trace of the correct behavior:

| Reading | window_sum | hard_violations | blocked |
|---------|-----------|-----------------|---------|
| 1       | 1.0       | 0               | False   |
| 2       | 2.0       | 0               | False   |
| 3       | 3.0 > 2.5 | 1               | False (warning) |
| 4       | 4.0 > 2.5 | 2               | False (warning) |
| 5       | 5.0 > 2.5 | 3               | **True** (HARD BLOCK) |

The clinical logic (HARD_BLOCK_VIOLATIONS = 3) is correct and unchanged.
Only the test assertion was wrong. Corrected to require 5 readings.

### Remaining open items (carried to v0.5.2)

- **[J3.4]** `requirements.txt`: add `scipy>=1.11,<2.0` version pin
- **[OI-007]** CPython heap persistence — mlock partial only (TPM 2.0: M1.5)

```markdown
# 🏗️ System Architecture: Cortex Protocol Framework
**Canonical Technical Reference — replaces INTENT-PROTOCOL.md**

This document is the single source of truth for the technical structure of the Cortex Protocol. It covers system layers, hardware topology, the intent-based interaction model, and the sovereignty loop. For the clinical evidence behind each design decision, see [CLINICAL-BRIDGE.md](../clinical/CLINICAL-BRIDGE.md) and [WHITE_PAPER.md](../clinical/WHITE_PAPER.md).

---

## 🧭 Design Philosophy: Protocol, Not OS

Cortex is not a traditional Operating System. It is a **Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL)**—a governance protocol that sits between hardware and the human, enforcing clinical and ethical constraints at the hardware level.

The user does not "open apps." The user declares an **Intent**. The Protocol delivers the **Result** while guaranteeing **Cognitive Sovereignty**.

Whether running on a mobile device, a high-end workstation, or a local edge server, the Acolyte orchestrates hardware resources (NPU, GPU, DSP, biometric sensors) in response to user intent, under the real-time supervision of cryptographically signed **Ethical Governance Nodes**.

---

## 🛰️ System Layers

The protocol is structured in four fundamental layers. Biometric and personal data never leave the device.

### Layer 1 — 🔩 Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL): *"The Body"*

The hardware interface. Handles all physical I/O and enforces the mathematical privacy transformation.

**Responsibilities:**
- Interfaces with any hardware architecture (ARM, x86, RISC-V) without vendor lock-in.
- Runs Local Inference Units (NPU/GPU) 100% locally. No cloud dependency.
- Manages the **Biosensor Hub**: low-latency access to HRV, EEG, GSR, and environmental sensors.
- Executes the two-phase tensor transformation: clinical feature extraction → HMAC obfuscation.
- Enforces GPG signature verification of Clinical Capability Modules at load time.

### Layer 2 — 🔢 Mathematical Privacy Layer: *"The Filter"*

Implements **Differential Privacy** principles (OpenMined/PySyft-inspired) to ensure the Acolyte learns from *patterns* without ever accessing raw biometric *values*.

**Key operations:**
- Normalization of raw signals to physiological reference ranges.
- Hilbert transform envelope extraction for dimensionality reduction.
- HMAC-SHA256 obfuscation with ephemeral per-session salt.
- Tensor encapsulation: all physiological inputs are converted to anonymous mathematical tensors before leaving the SAL boundary.

**Privacy guarantee:** The Mathematical Privacy Layer ensures that even a compromised Acolyte cannot reconstruct the user's raw biometric state from the tensors it receives.

### Layer 3 — 🤖 Master Agent Core (The Acolyte): *"The Mind"*

The central AI agent. Built on local Small Language Models (SLMs) optimized for edge silicon.

**Responsibilities:**
- **Intent Orchestrator:** Parses user intent and allocates hardware resources without intermediate app layers. Compatible with local inference engines: Llama.cpp, ExecuTorch, Whisper.
- **Cognitive State Engine:** Analyzes anonymized tensors to classify mental load states (Flow, Stress, Overload) using the Polyvagal state mapping from the Clinical Bridge.
- **Ethical Sandbox:** Every Acolyte decision is cross-referenced against GPG-signed rulesets from Governance Nodes before hardware execution. If rulesets are missing or invalid, the capability module is blocked.

**What the Acolyte never sees:**
- Raw biometric values (EEG amplitude, HRV intervals, GSR).
- The session salt used for HMAC obfuscation.
- The Phase A clinical features before obfuscation.

### Layer 4 — 🖥️ Sovereign Neural Interface (SNI): *"The Senses"*

The adaptive user interface layer. Replaces static app grids with intent-driven, clinically-aware environments.

**Capabilities:**
- **Adaptive UX:** Visual complexity adjusts based on detected cognitive load state.
- **Sensory Buffer:** Hardware-level modulation of screen Hz, blue light temperature, and audio frequencies to maintain autonomic homeostasis.
- **Sovereign Kill-Switch:** The user can override any Protocol decision at any point. Human sovereignty is unconditional.

---

## 🔄 The Sovereignty Loop (Privacy by Design)

The full processing cycle for each biometric frame:

```
[User Intent / Biometric Sensor Input]
           ↓
[SAL: Sensor Certification Handshake]
    ↙ Rejected        ↘ Certified
[Block]          [Phase A: Clinical Feature Extraction]
                           ↓
                 [Clinical Bridge Validation]
                   ↙ Violation   ↘ Cleared
                [Block]     [Phase B: HMAC Obfuscation]
                                       ↓
                            [Acolyte: Tensor Processing]
                                       ↓
                         [CDI: Drift Detection Update]
                           ↙ Drift         ↘ Safe
                    [Block/Alert]     [Hardware Execution]
                                           ↓
                              [Result delivered to user]
```

**All processing is local. All data stays on the device.**

---

## 🧰 Technical Stack

| Component | Library / Tool | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Local Inference** | Llama.cpp / ExecuTorch | High-performance local LLM/SLM execution on edge silicon |
| **EEG/Biometric Processing** | NumPy / MNE-Python | Signal normalization, Hilbert transform, feature extraction |
| **Audio (therapeutic)** | PipeWire / Oboe | Low-latency, universal audio orchestration |
| **Spatial Audio** | Resonance Audio / libmysofa | 3D sound field rendering for therapeutic use |
| **Cryptography** | Python `hmac`, `hashlib`, `secrets` | Session salt generation, HMAC-SHA256 tensor obfuscation |
| **Governance Signing** | GPG / OpenPGP | Digital signatures for Clinical Capability Modules |
| **Trusted Execution** | OP-TEE / TPM 2.0 | Secure local storage of manifests and user keys |
| **Privacy Layer** | OpenMined / PySyft (roadmap) | Federated learning for population-level CDI refinement |

---

## 🔐 Ethical Governance Mechanism

Governance Nodes do not merely audit documents — they control what the Acolyte can physically execute at runtime.

**Constitutional System Prompts:** Ethical constraints are loaded into the Acolyte's context as Constitutional Law before any intent processing begins.

**Signed Manifests:** Constraints are structured text files, validated and digitally signed by independent Governance Nodes (university faculties, professional associations).

**Hardware Enforcement:** The SAL verifies GPG signatures at module load time. If the signature is absent or invalid, the Protocol refuses to activate the capability module — regardless of Acolyte instructions.

**Annual Review Cycle:** Signed manifests are time-limited and require renewal after peer review. A manifest that has not been reviewed in 12 months is automatically downgraded to advisory-only status.

| **4 (2030+)** | Federated Governance Network | University node network; federated CDI refinement |

B2. NEUTRALITY.md — Cognitive Neutrality Doctrine [KEY]
------------------------------------------------------------------------

```markdown
# NEUTRALITY.md
## Cognitive Neutrality Architecture — Canonical Doctrine
**Document ID: ARCH-NEUTRALITY-001 | Version: 1.0**
**Cortex Protocol — Protocol Stewards & White Branch**
**Status: Normative — referenced by STANDARD.md, CONSTITUTION.md, GOVERNANCE.md**

---

> *"Neutrality is not the absence of opinion. It is the structural impossibility of injecting one."*

---

## Preamble

This document formally defines the **Cognitive Neutrality Clause** of the Cortex Protocol — the architectural invariant that prevents any institutional, political, commercial, or ideological actor from using the protocol's own infrastructure to influence the cognitive state of its users.

The Cognitive Neutrality Clause is not a policy declaration. Policies can be changed by actors with sufficient authority. The Clause is a **mathematical and architectural constraint** enforced at the code level, whose violation requires rewriting core modules, not amending a terms-of-service document.

This is the foundational distinction between the Cortex Protocol and every privacy policy, clinical ethics board, and AI safety framework that preceded it: **we do not ask institutions to behave neutrally. We make non-neutral behavior technically impossible by design.**

This document:
1. Defines Cognitive Neutrality as a formal architectural invariant (§1)
2. Maps each enforcement mechanism to its implementing module (§2)
3. Introduces the **Split-Gate Doctrine** — the dual-mode operational architecture for research and commercial deployments (§3)
4. Catalogs the residual honest vulnerabilities that the current architecture does not fully close (§4)
5. Specifies the governance process for modifications to this doctrine (§5)

---

## §1 — Cognitive Neutrality: Formal Definition

### 1.1 The Invariant

**Cognitive Neutrality** is satisfied if and only if:

```
∀ message m transmitted over the Cortex P2P fabric:
  semanticContent(m) = ∅

∀ rule r loaded into the External Rule Sandbox:
  output(r) ∈ ℤ ∩ [0, 100]  OR  output(r) ∈ MitigationVector
  ∧  IOCapability(r) = ∅
  ∧  NetworkCapability(r) = ∅

∀ query q submitted to the Data Pool:
  geographicDimension(q) = ∅
  ∧  demographicDimension(q) = ∅
  ∧  eventCorrelation(q) = ∅
```

In plain language: the network cannot carry meaning, rules cannot reach outside themselves, and the data pool has no spatial or social coordinates. Each of these is enforced structurally, not contractually.

### 1.2 What Neutrality Prohibits

The following capabilities **do not exist** in the Cortex Protocol — not because they are disallowed, but because the architecture has no mechanism to implement them:

| Capability | Why it cannot exist |
|---|---|
| Broadcasting an institutional health alert | `CortexMsgType` has no alert type. The parser drops unknown types silently at byte 2. |
| Sending "this region shows elevated stress" | `DataPoolReadPort.query()` has no geographic parameter. Passing one raises `ValueError` before any data is accessed. |
| Injecting a behavioral recommendation via P2P | `ImmuneSignaturePayload` has no text field. Maximum payload is 66 bytes of typed integers and hashes. |
| Loading a rule that calls an external API | `ExternalRuleSandbox` shadows `socket`, `urllib`, `requests` with `_NoOpProxy`. The call returns empty silently. |
| Modifying clinical thresholds without quorum | `white_branch_threshold.py` requires N=5 of M=9 signatures across ≥3 independent jurisdictions. |
| Identifying the geographic origin of a biometric vector | `PoolEntry` has no geographic field. The schema cannot be extended without a White Branch MAJOR version increment. |

### 1.3 What Neutrality Permits

Cognitive Neutrality is not silence. The protocol carries meaningful technical signals:

- Anonymous biometric feature vectors (`ANONYMOUS_VECTOR`) — mathematical, not interpretive
- Node liveness signals (`SENSOR_HEARTBEAT`) — protocol telemetry only
- Technical threat signatures (`IMMUNE_SIGNATURE`) — cryptographic hashes of protocol violations, never semantic descriptions
- Clinical capability modules (`GOVERNANCE_CCM`) — affect physiological thresholds only, signed by multi-party governance quorum
- Key rotation announcements (`KEY_ROTATION`) — session cryptography maintenance
- Routing table updates (`ROUTING_TABLE_UPDATE`) — network topology, no content

This is the complete vocabulary. Adding a type requires a MAJOR version increment, a White Branch clinical review, and a threshold signature from ≥5 Governance Nodes.

---

## §2 — Enforcement Map: Invariant to Module

Each component of the Cognitive Neutrality invariant is enforced by a specific module. This section maps the formal invariant to its implementation, creating an auditable chain from doctrine to code.

### 2.1 P2P Closed Vocabulary

**Invariant enforced:** `semanticContent(m) = ∅` for all P2P messages.

**Module:** `src/p2p/p2p_message_types.py` — `CortexPacketParser`

**Mechanism:** The parser maintains a `frozenset` of valid type bytes (`0x01`–`0x06`). Any packet whose type byte is not in this set is dropped silently at byte 2 of parsing — before deserialization, before logging, before any application logic. There is no error returned to the caller. The packet does not exist.

The `ImmuneSignaturePayload` struct (66 bytes) has no string field, no label field, no description field. The 256-byte maximum for `IMMUNE_SIGNATURE` packets is a structural ceiling: it is physically impossible to encode a paragraph of interpretive text in 66 bytes of typed integers.

**Verification:** `python3 -m src.p2p.p2p_message_types` — Test 2 demonstrates that type `0xFF` (simulating `INSTITUTIONAL_ALERT`) is silently dropped with zero exception propagation.

### 2.2 Geographic Blind Spot

**Invariant enforced:** `geographicDimension(q) = ∅` for all Data Pool queries and responses.

**Module:** `src/p2p/data_pool.py` — `DataPoolReadPort.query()`

**Mechanism:** The `query()` method accepts only parameters in `ALLOWED_QUERY_PARAMS = frozenset({"clinical_domain", "time_window_days", "limit", "anonymization_proof_required"})`. Any `**kwargs` are checked against this set before any data access occurs. A query with `geographic_region="EU"` raises `ValueError` with a message explaining that this is a structural protection, not a data quality limitation.

The `PoolEntry` dataclass has no geographic field. The `to_dict()` serialization method explicitly documents the absent fields. The `StagingBucket` key is `(ClinicalDomain, polyvagal_bucket)` — there is no geographic component in the grouping key, so vectors from different regions are mixed within the same k-anonymity bucket before release.

**k-Anonymity gate:** No single vector is released in isolation. Vectors are held until k ≥ 5 statistically similar vectors from distinct sessions are available. A consumer receiving a batch cannot determine the geographic distribution of contributors.

**Verification:** `python3 -m src.p2p.data_pool` — Test 1 demonstrates that `geographic_region="EU"` raises `ValueError` before any data is accessed.

### 2.3 External Rule Isolation

**Invariant enforced:** `IOCapability(r) = ∅ ∧ NetworkCapability(r) = ∅` for all external rules.

**Module:** `src/sal/external_rule_sandbox.py` — `ExternalRuleSandbox`, `_build_restricted_globals()`

**Mechanism:** Rules execute inside a restricted namespace constructed by `_build_restricted_globals()`. Every I/O builtin (`open`, `print`, `input`, `exec`, `eval`) is replaced by `_NoOpProxy` — a null object that absorbs any call silently and returns empty values. Every networking module (`socket`, `urllib`, `requests`, `httpx`) is replaced by `_NoOpProxy`.

Thread spawning (`threading.Thread`) is replaced by `_ForbiddenProxy` which raises `SandboxViolation` immediately and permanently blacklists the rule. The distinction is intentional: silent failures allow a malformed rule to run to completion; active violations (threading) are structurally dangerous and require hard termination.

Rules have a 50ms execution timeout enforced via `threading.Timer`. Rules that exceed this are marked as faulted; after 3 faults, the rule is suspended pending governance review.

The return value contract is strict: only `int ∈ [0, 100]` or `MitigationVector` are accepted. Anything else (including `bool`, `str`, `float`) returns score=0 (BLOCKED). This prevents rules from encoding side-channels in exotic return types.

**Verification:** `python3 -m src.sal.external_rule_sandbox` — Tests 3 and 4 demonstrate I/O silent neutralization and thread blacklisting respectively.

### 2.4 Anti-Sybil Defense (Immune Network)

**Invariant enforced:** No single node can inject a false immune signal into the network.

**Module:** `src/p2p/immune_network.py` — `ImmuneNetworkNode`, `CoSignatureAccumulator`

**Mechanism:** Three-layer defense:

- **Layer 1 (Rate Limiting):** Each node may emit ≤3 `IMMUNE_SIGNATURE` messages per hour. A node controlling N fake identities must generate N × 3 messages per hour, bounded by the contribution requirement.
- **Layer 2 (Contribution Staking):** A node must have contributed ≥50 anonymous vectors to the Data Pool before its immune signatures are forwarded. Cost of Sybil attack: N identities × 50 real biometric sessions each.
- **Layer 3 (Threshold Co-signing):** An `IMMUNE_SIGNATURE` is only propagated when K=3 independent staked nodes co-sign the same `evidence_hash` within a 5-minute window. A single compromised node cannot trigger propagation.

**Verification:** `python3 -m src.p2p.immune_network` — Test 4 demonstrates that 1 and 2 co-signers are insufficient; the threshold requires 3.

### 2.5 Clinical Threshold Governance

**Invariant enforced:** Clinical thresholds cannot be modified by any single institutional actor.

**Module:** `src/governance/white_branch_threshold.py`

**Mechanism:** Modifications to clinical thresholds require N=5 of M=9 multi-party threshold signatures, with a mandatory requirement that signatories span ≥3 independent jurisdictions. This prevents any single nation-state, regulatory body, or corporate actor from unilaterally redefining what constitutes a safe or unsafe physiological state.

The threshold parameters (N, M, minimum jurisdictions) are themselves governed by the same process — they cannot be reduced without the quorum they define.

### 2.6 Physical Bus Encryption

**Invariant enforced:** The host OS cannot read raw biometric data in transit from sensor to TEE.

**Module:** `src/keros/sensor_channel.py` — `SensorEndpoint`, `TEEEndpoint`, `SecureBusSession`

**Mechanism:** Full ECDH handshake with X25519 ephemeral keys per session. HKDF-SHA256 key derivation using the TEE's challenge nonce as salt (domain separation). Frame-level ChaCha20-Poly1305 AEAD encryption with strictly increasing `frame_seq` in AEAD additional data (anti-replay + anti-reordering).

The SensorAck (HMAC of challenge under session key) closes the MITM vector: an attacker substituting the TEE's public key will cause the sensor to derive a different session key, and the SensorAck will fail verification at the TEE. The session is not established.

After a `FrameAuthError` (Poly1305 MAC failure), the session is marked `COMPROMISED` and no further frames are processed. This is the correct response to active bus tampering.

---

## §3 — The Split-Gate Doctrine

The Split-Gate Doctrine formally defines the two operational modes of the Cortex Protocol and specifies the cryptographic conditions under which each mode activates. This doctrine is the technical answer to a fundamental tension in the protocol: scientific research requires access to higher-fidelity data under controlled conditions, while consumer deployment requires the strongest possible protections without exception.

The resolution is architectural: **the same codebase operates in two distinct modes, separated by a cryptographic gate that neither the user nor the developer can bypass unilaterally.**

### 3.1 Mode I — Research Mode (Bypass Gate)

**Activation condition:** Explicit cryptographic consent from the research subject + countersignature from an active Governance Node.

**Technical gate:**
```
ResearchBypassToken = Sign(
    subject_public_key,
    {
        "session_id":     <SHA-256 of session>,
        "bypass_scope":   ["phi_filter", "k_anonymity"],  // explicit list
        "expiry_ts":      <Unix timestamp, max 8 hours>,
        "study_id":       <Governance Node registered study identifier>,
        "governance_sig": <Threshold signature from ≥2 Governance Nodes>
    }
)
```

**What Research Mode permits:**
- Φ filter bypass: higher-fidelity feature vectors available to the research pipeline, still within the TEE boundary
- k-anonymity bypass: individual session vectors released to a closed research endpoint with explicit subject consent
- Extended session TTL for longitudinal studies

**What Research Mode does NOT permit:**
- Disabling the ECDH physical bus encryption
- Disabling the P2P closed vocabulary enforcement
- Disabling the HMAC authentication on Data Pool entries
- Reducing the White Branch threshold signature quorum
- Removing the External Rule Sandbox isolation

The Φ filter and k-anonymity gate are the only components that can be bypassed under Research Mode. Every other protection is invariant across both modes.

**Auditability requirement:** Every Research Mode session generates a cryptographically signed audit entry that cannot be deleted without the subject's private key. The subject retains the right to request deletion of their session data at any time, with the audit entry recording the deletion.

### 3.2 Mode II — Commercial Mode (Immutable Filter)

**Activation condition:** Default. No token required. No action required by user or developer.

**Technical gate:** Absence of a valid `ResearchBypassToken`. The SAL pipeline checks for the token at initialization; if absent or invalid, Commercial Mode is enforced.

**What Commercial Mode enforces:**
- Φ filter: mandatory, non-bypassable. All biometric data passes through Daubechies-2 wavelet decomposition + homeostatic noise injection before any downstream processing.
- k-anonymity: mandatory. No individual session vector is released from the Data Pool without k ≥ 5 grouping.
- External Rule Sandbox: mandatory. No external rule can bypass the I/O and network isolation.
- ZKP proofs: every Data Pool entry carries an anonymization proof verifiable by consumers.
- Session TTL: maximum 4 hours, enforced by `ClinicalSessionKey`.

**The consumer protection guarantee:** A developer building a consumer application on the Cortex Protocol cannot, through any SDK configuration or API call, disable Commercial Mode protections. The only path to reduced protections is a Governance Node-signed Research Mode token — which requires a registered study and subject consent.

This is the structural defense against the most likely attack vector: a well-intentioned developer who, under commercial pressure, "temporarily" disables a protection "just for this use case."

### 3.3 The Gate Is Cryptographic, Not Contractual

The distinction between Research Mode and Commercial Mode is enforced by the presence or absence of a valid `ResearchBypassToken` — a cryptographic object that requires:

1. The subject's signature (cannot be forged without the subject's private key)
2. A countersignature from ≥2 active Governance Nodes (cannot be forged without compromising governance key infrastructure)
3. A valid study registration (cannot be fabricated without governance registry access)

No SDK configuration flag, no environment variable, no developer override can activate Research Mode without this token. This is the cryptographic gate.

---

## §4 — Residual Honest Vulnerabilities

The Cortex Protocol is committed to publishing its own attack surface honestly. The following vulnerabilities are known, partially mitigated, and openly documented. Their presence does not invalidate the protocol — it defines the engineering roadmap.

### 4.1 Physical Sensor-to-TEE Bus (Partially Closed)

**Status:** Partially closed by `sensor_channel.py` (v0.4.0).

**Residual risk:** The ECDH handshake and ChaCha20-Poly1305 frame encryption protect the logical bus. However, an attacker with physical access to the board who can probe the ADC output pins before the sensor's firmware encrypts the data operates below the cryptographic layer. This is a hardware threat that software cannot fully close.

**Production mitigation path:** Sensors with on-chip secure enclaves (e.g., ARM Cortex-M33 with TrustZone-M) can perform the ECDH handshake inside the sensor's secure world, so plaintext never appears on any external pin. This is the Milestone 2 hardware target.

**Current status:** PoC accepts that the sensor microcontroller is trusted. Production deployments in clinical environments must specify a certified sensor hardware profile.

### 4.2 CPython Heap Key Persistence

**Status:** Known limitation, documented in `OPEN_ISSUES.md` [OI-007] and `SECURITY.md §6`.

**Residual risk:** Python `bytes` objects are immutable. When `ClinicalSessionKey.zeroize()` or `SecureBusSession.close()` overwrite the session key reference, the CPython garbage collector may retain the original `bytes` object in heap memory until the next GC cycle. An attacker with read access to process memory (e.g., via `/proc/<pid>/mem`) can recover session key material.

**Production mitigation path:** KEROS TPM 2.0 hardware integration (Milestone 1.5). All encryption operations performed inside the Secure Enclave. Session keys are generated, used, and destroyed entirely within TPM-protected memory. The Python layer only holds handles, not key material.

**Current status:** Acceptable for PoC validation. Unacceptable for clinical deployment without KEROS hardware integration.

### 4.3 The White Branch as Long-Horizon Capture Target

**Status:** Acknowledged architectural constraint. Partially mitigated by threshold governance design.

**Residual risk:** The White Branch is composed of human institutions. Over a multi-decade horizon, the institutions that constitute the White Branch can be captured by state actors, commercial interests, or ideological movements. A captured White Branch that controls N=5 of the M=9 Governance Nodes could issue Clinical Capability Modules that redefine clinical thresholds to serve non-clinical purposes.

**Structural mitigations currently in place:**
- The ≥3 independent jurisdictions requirement makes simultaneous capture of a quorum significantly more difficult
- CCM version history is immutable in git — all threshold modifications are publicly auditable
- The Constitution establishes that threshold modifications must carry bibliographic citations to peer-reviewed literature
- Any Governance Node can publish a dissent record against any CCM

**Residual risk that cannot be closed by architecture alone:** If the peer-reviewed literature itself is systematically biased, or if all three jurisdictions are simultaneously subject to the same political pressure, the bibliographic citation requirement provides no defense. This is the fundamental limit of any trust architecture: there is a level of systemic capture below which no cryptographic protocol can provide protection.

**Honest acknowledgment:** Cortex's defense against this risk is transparency and time. The public auditability of all threshold changes, combined with the 48-hour propagation delay for CCMs, creates a window for community review and objection. This is not a cryptographic guarantee — it is a social mechanism, and social mechanisms have failure modes.

### 4.4 Sandbox Namespace Isolation (PoC Limitation)

**Status:** Known limitation, flagged in `external_rule_sandbox.py` docstring.

**Residual risk:** The current sandbox implementation uses Python namespace shadowing to isolate external rules. This is not equivalent to true WASM linear memory isolation. A sufficiently determined rule author with knowledge of CPython internals could potentially escape the namespace restriction through bytecode manipulation or `ctypes` calls that bypass the restricted globals.

**Production mitigation path:** Milestone 2 target is actual WASM sandbox execution via Pyodide or Wasmtime, with linear memory limits enforced by the runtime. At that point, escape requires a WASM runtime vulnerability, not just Python knowledge.

**Current status:** Acceptable for PoC with rules authored by trusted Governance Node institutions. Unacceptable for rules sourced from untrusted third parties without WASM sandbox enforcement.

---

## §5 — Modification Governance

### 5.1 What Requires Modification of This Document

The following changes to the Cortex Protocol require an amendment to this document and a MAJOR version increment of `STANDARD.md`:

- Adding a new `CortexMsgType` value
- Modifying the `ALLOWED_QUERY_PARAMS` set in `DataPoolReadPort`
- Changing the k-anonymity minimum (currently k=5)
- Adding a new `ImmunePatternType` or `ImmuneSignatureScope`
- Changing the Research Mode bypass token structure
- Modifying the White Branch quorum parameters (N, M, jurisdiction minimum)
- Closing any of the residual vulnerabilities in §4 (requires documentation of the new architecture)

### 5.2 Amendment Process

Amendments to this document follow the same process as amendments to `STANDARD.md`:

1. RFC published as a GitHub Issue tagged `[RFC-Neutrality-Amendment]`
2. 30-day public comment period
3. White Branch clinical review (for any change affecting biometric data handling)
4. Threshold signature from ≥5 Governance Nodes spanning ≥3 jurisdictions
5. MAJOR version increment
6. Updated `CHANGELOG.md` entry with full diff summary

No amendment may reduce the structural enforcement mechanisms in §2 to policy-based mechanisms. The requirement that enforcement be architectural is itself unamendable by design — doing so would require rewriting the codebase in a way that is publicly visible and auditable.

### 5.3 Emergency Amendment Protocol

In the event that a critical security vulnerability is discovered in one of the enforcement mechanisms in §2, the following expedited process applies:

1. Vulnerability disclosed to Protocol Stewards under coordinated disclosure
2. 72-hour window for patch development
3. Threshold signature from ≥3 Governance Nodes (reduced quorum for emergency)
4. Public disclosure simultaneously with patch release
5. Full amendment process (§5.2) completed within 30 days of emergency patch

The reduced quorum for emergency amendments (≥3 vs. ≥5) is justified by the time constraint. The 30-day follow-up with full quorum ensures that emergency patches are not used to permanently reduce governance requirements.

---

## §6 — Relationship to Other Protocol Documents

This document is **normative** and is referenced by:

| Document | Dependency |
|---|---|
| `STANDARD.md` | §2 (enforcement map) is the technical specification backing STANDARD.md Part II |
| `CONSTITUTION.md` | §1 (formal invariant) is the technical specification of Article 2 (Absolute Prohibition of Capture Asymmetry) |
| `GOVERNANCE.md` | §5 (modification governance) extends GOVERNANCE.md §4 for neutrality-specific amendments |
| `OPEN_ISSUES.md` | §4 (residual vulnerabilities) is the authoritative source for [OI-001] through [OI-004] as they relate to neutrality |
| `ARCHITECTURE.md` | §2 (enforcement map) extends ARCHITECTURE.md's Sovereignty Loop with cryptographic specificity |

This document does **not** replace any of the above. It provides the canonical link between the protocol's philosophical commitments (CONSTITUTION.md, MANIFESTO.md) and the specific modules that enforce them (the implementation).

---

## Appendix A — Glossary of Neutrality-Specific Terms

**Cognitive Neutrality Clause:** The architectural invariant defined in §1.1. Refers to the ensemble of structural mechanisms that prevent semantic content from entering the P2P fabric.

**Split-Gate Doctrine:** The dual-mode operational architecture defined in §3. Research Mode and Commercial Mode are the two gates; the cryptographic token is the gate mechanism.

**Research Mode:** Operational mode activated by a valid `ResearchBypassToken`. Permits Φ filter and k-anonymity bypass under controlled conditions.

**Commercial Mode:** Default operational mode. All §2 enforcement mechanisms active. No bypass available without a Governance Node-countersigned token.

**Structural Enforcement:** A protection that is enforced by the absence of a code path capable of violating it, as opposed to policy enforcement, which is enforced by rules that prohibit exercising an existing code path.

**Geographic Blind Spot:** The architectural property of the Data Pool that makes it structurally impossible to query or receive data with a geographic dimension. Implemented by `DataPoolReadPort.ALLOWED_QUERY_PARAMS` and the absence of geographic fields in `PoolEntry`.

**Residual Honest Vulnerability:** A known limitation of the current implementation that the protocol acknowledges publicly and is committed to addressing in a defined milestone. The list in §4 is maintained as a living section of this document.

---

*Amendments require White Branch review and threshold signature per §5.2.*

B3. ARCHITECTURE-ASYNC.md
------------------------------------------------------------------------

```markdown
## Asynchronous Architecture: Solving the Biological-AI Latency Asymmetry

**Document ID: ARCH-ASYNC-001 | Version: 1.0**
**Relates to:** [ARCHITECTURE.md](ARCHITECTURE.md) — extends the Sovereignty Loop section.

---

## The Problem: Speed Asymmetry

The Cortex Protocol mediates between two systems that operate at fundamentally different timescales:

| System | Timescale | Example |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| AI agent (Acolyte) | Milliseconds | Token generation, inference, response |
| Biometric sensor (HRV, GSR) | Seconds | Heart rate update, HRV window calculation |
| Governance Node validation | Minutes to hours | Policy snapshot refresh |

**If the AI pipeline waits for synchronous biometric validation on every request, the system becomes unusable.** A 2-second HRV update cycle would introduce 2-second latency into every AI interaction. At scale, this collapses the user experience and defeats the protocol's purpose.

This is a known architectural constraint, not an oversight. This document specifies the required solution.

---

## The Solution: Three Non-Negotiable Design Decisions

### Decision 1 — Separated Threads (Async Processing)

The AI pipeline and the biometric reader run in completely independent threads or processes. They never block each other.

```
Thread A: Biometric Reader
  Sensor → Feature Extraction → CDI Update → State Buffer Write

Thread B: AI Pipeline
  User Request → State Buffer Read → Acolyte → Response

Thread A and Thread B NEVER call each other directly.
Communication happens ONLY through the State Buffer.
```

This separation is architectural law. Any implementation that introduces synchronous coupling between Thread A and Thread B violates the protocol's latency requirements.

### Decision 2 — Local Biological State Buffer

The system maintains a local, in-memory state object that the AI pipeline can read with zero network latency. The biometric thread updates it asynchronously in the background.

**Required structure of the State Buffer:**

```python
@dataclass
class BiometricStateBuffer:
    status: str           # "SAFE" | "WARNING" | "BLOCKED"
    polyvagal_state: str  # "ventral_vagal" | "sympathetic" | "dorsal_vagal"
    coherency_index: float
    timestamp: float      # Unix timestamp of last real sensor reading
    sensor_hmac: bytes    # HMAC(status + timestamp, sensor_session_key)
    ttl_seconds: int = 5  # State expires if sensor goes silent

    def is_valid(self) -> bool:
        """
        Two conditions must BOTH be true for state to be trusted:
        1. Timestamp is recent (sensor is alive)
        2. HMAC is valid (state was written by authenticated sensor thread)
        If either fails → treat as BLOCKED (safe-fail, not fail-open)
        """
        if time.time() - self.timestamp > self.ttl_seconds:
            return False  # Sensor silent — fail safe
        expected_hmac = hmac.new(
            SENSOR_SESSION_KEY,
            f"{self.status}{self.timestamp}".encode(),
            hashlib.sha256
        ).digest()
        return hmac.compare_digest(expected_hmac, self.sensor_hmac)
```

**Critical constraint:** Only the authenticated biometric thread may write to the State Buffer. The AI pipeline is read-only. This must be enforced at the process level, not by convention.

### Decision 3 — Local Policy Snapshot

Clinical thresholds and CDI rules are downloaded once per day from the active Governance Node as a cryptographically signed package. All validation runs locally — no network round-trip per request.

**Required snapshot structure:**

```json
{
  "version": 42,
  "issued_at": 1748000000,
  "expires_at": 1748086400,
  "issuer_node": "governance-node-[node-identifier]",
  "thresholds": {
    "bridge_std_limit": 0.5,
    "bridge_p75_limit": 0.7,
    "bridge_max_limit": 0.9,
    "max_coherency_sum_per_minute": 2.5,
    "hard_block_violations": 3,
    "soft_block_violations": 5
  },
  "signature": "<GPG signature of above content>"
}
```

**Validation rules for the snapshot:**
- Reject if GPG signature is invalid.
- Reject if `version` is lower than the last accepted version (prevents replay attacks with older, less restrictive policies).
- Reject if `expires_at` has passed.
- On rejection, continue using the last valid snapshot. Do not fail open.

---

## Known Vulnerabilities — Developers Must Address These

These are not theoretical. They are exploitable if not resolved.

### Vulnerability 1 — State Buffer Injection (Critical)

**Attack:** A malicious process writes `status = "SAFE"` directly to the State Buffer, bypassing the biometric thread entirely.

**Mitigation:** The HMAC in the State Buffer (Decision 2 above) makes this detectable. The AI pipeline must always call `is_valid()` before trusting the state. A forged state cannot produce a valid HMAC without the sensor session key.

**Additional mitigation:** On Linux/macOS, the state buffer process should use OS-level memory protection (e.g., `mprotect` with write restriction for the AI process). On mobile, use the platform's Secure Enclave for the sensor session key.

### Vulnerability 2 — Silent Sensor Failure (Critical)

**Attack / failure mode:** The sensor disconnects or stops transmitting. The State Buffer retains the last state indefinitely. If that state was `SAFE`, the AI continues operating without any biometric oversight.

**Mitigation:** The TTL field in the State Buffer (5 seconds default). If the biometric thread has not written a fresh state within TTL, `is_valid()` returns False, which the Circuit Breaker treats as BLOCKED. Silence equals block — never silence equals safe.

### Vulnerability 3 — Policy Snapshot Replay Attack (High)

**Attack:** An attacker captures a valid snapshot with permissive thresholds (e.g., from a period before thresholds were tightened) and re-injects it.

**Mitigation:** The monotonic `version` field. The client stores the last accepted version number in persistent local storage. Any snapshot with a lower or equal version number to the currently active one is rejected, even if the signature is valid.

### Vulnerability 4 — Race Condition on State Buffer Write/Read (Medium)

**Attack / failure mode:** The biometric thread writes `BLOCKED` to the buffer at the exact moment the AI thread reads `SAFE` — the AI reads stale state.

**Mitigation:** Use atomic operations for the status field. In Python: `threading.Event` or `asyncio.Lock` wrapping the buffer write. The window of vulnerability without this is microseconds — small but nonzero and exploitable under high-frequency sensor updates.

---

## Required Design Patterns

These are not suggestions. They are the implementation contract for any developer building on this architecture.

### Pattern 1 — Circuit Breaker (Primary Safety Mechanism)

Wraps every call to the Acolyte. If the State Buffer is invalid, expired, or BLOCKED, the Circuit Breaker opens and the request never reaches the AI.

```python
class BiometricCircuitBreaker:
    """
    Three states:
    CLOSED  → normal operation, buffer valid and SAFE
    OPEN    → blocked, buffer invalid/expired/BLOCKED
    HALF-OPEN → testing recovery after a block period
    """

    def __init__(self, state_buffer: BiometricStateBuffer):
        self.buffer = state_buffer
        self._circuit = "CLOSED"

    def call(self, acolyte_fn, *args, **kwargs):
        if not self.buffer.is_valid():
            self._circuit = "OPEN"
            raise BiometricStateExpiredError(
                "Sensor data expired or invalid — safe fail engaged"
            )

        if self.buffer.status == "BLOCKED":
            self._circuit = "OPEN"
            raise CDIBlockError(
                f"CDI threshold exceeded — polyvagal state: "
                f"{self.buffer.polyvagal_state}"
            )

        self._circuit = "CLOSED"
        return acolyte_fn(*args, **kwargs)
```

### Pattern 2 — Observer with Unidirectional Channel

The biometric thread publishes state change events to a channel. The AI thread subscribes passively. No direct calls between threads in either direction.

```
Biometric Thread  →  [Event Queue]  →  State Buffer
AI Thread         ←reads only from←   State Buffer

Rule: AI Thread NEVER writes to State Buffer.
Rule: State Buffer NEVER calls AI Thread.
Rule: Biometric Thread NEVER calls AI Thread directly.
```

This eliminates circular dependencies and makes the system's behavior under concurrency easy to reason about.

### Pattern 3 — Snapshot Pattern for Policies

The daily policy snapshot is treated as an immutable versioned object. It is never mutated in memory. When a new snapshot arrives:

1. Validate the new snapshot (signature, version, expiry).
2. If valid, create a new snapshot object.
3. Atomic swap: replace the reference to the active snapshot.
4. Keep the previous snapshot in memory during a grace period for in-flight sessions.
5. Discard the previous snapshot after the grace period.

No session ever operates on a partially-updated policy set.

### Pattern 4 — CQRS for the Audit Log

The session audit log uses Command Query Responsibility Segregation:

- **Write side (Commands):** append-only, immutable. Biometric events, CDI decisions, block events, consent changes are written here and never modified.
- **Read side (Queries):** indexed projections of the write log for fast queries by the user or forensic review.

This satisfies the STANDARD.md audit log requirements and ensures that any security incident is fully reconstructible.

---

## Implementation Checklist for Developers

Before submitting a pull request that touches the async pipeline, verify:

- [ ] Biometric thread and AI thread have zero direct calls between them
- [ ] State Buffer writes are atomic and protected from concurrent access
- [ ] State Buffer `is_valid()` checks both HMAC and TTL before returning trusted state
- [ ] Circuit Breaker is the sole entry point to Acolyte invocation
- [ ] Sensor silence (TTL expiry) defaults to BLOCKED, not SAFE
- [ ] Policy snapshot validation checks: GPG signature, version monotonicity, expiry
- [ ] Audit log is append-only on the write side
- [ ] No network call occurs in the synchronous AI request path

---

| Document | Relationship |
| :--- | :--- |
| [ARCHITECTURE.md](ARCHITECTURE.md) | Parent document — this extends the Sovereignty Loop section |

B4. MODULE-ISOLATION.md
------------------------------------------------------------------------

```markdown
# 🔒 Module Isolation Protocol: Sovereign Sandboxing

### Structural Security and Zero-Trust Architecture for Capability Modules
This document defines how the **Cortex Protocol** isolates Clinical Capability Modules (CCM) from each other. Isolation is not a feature; it is a structural mandate to prevent a compromised or malfunctioning module from accessing data or hardware resources belonging to another domain.

---

## 🧭 Design Philosophy: Zero-Trust Introspection

In a traditional OS, apps share system services freely. In the Cortex Protocol, every module is treated as an **untrusted component** by default, even after certification by an Ethical Governance Node.
**The principle:** A compromised audio module must never be able to read HRV data. A compromised biometric module must never be able to inject audio. No exceptions. This is the technical enforcement of the **Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL)**.

---

## 🏗️ The Isolation Framework (Agnostic Implementation)
The protocol ensures isolation across different hardware environments (Mobile, Desktop, Edge) by utilizing the best available local security primitive:

### 1. Data Path Segregation
- **Encapsulated Channels:** Communication between the **Acolyte** (Core Agent) and any module occurs through strictly defined, encrypted IPC (Inter-Process Communication) channels.
- **No Cross-Talk:** Modules are physically prohibited from communicating with each other. All data must pass through the Acolyte's ethical filter.

### 2. Resource Quotas & Sandboxing
- **Compute Limits:** Every module is assigned a specific quota of GPU/NPU/CPU cycles to prevent "Denial of Service" attacks on the user's focus.
- **Memory Zeroing:** The protocol mandates that any memory used by a clinical module for processing biometric data is zeroed out immediately after the task is completed.

---

## 🛤️ Evolution of Isolation (Hardware Roadmap)
The protocol scales its security based on the hardware it is running on:
- **Standard Isolation (Software Level):** Uses OS-level process isolation (UIDs, Namespaces, and Cgroups) to create a "sandbox" for each module.
- **Enhanced Isolation (Hardware Level):** On supported hardware (e.g., ARMv9 with CCA or modern x86 with Secure Enclaves), the protocol runs modules within **Trusted Execution Environments (TEE)**.
- **Cryptographic Attestation:** In advanced deployments, the protocol verifies the digital signature of the module's code before allowing it to access the **Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL)**.

---

## 🚨 Anomaly Detection & Breach Response
The **Acolyte** constantly monitors module behavior. If a module attempts to exceed its boundaries, the response is graduated and enforced by the Protocol:

| Severity | Detected Behavior | Protocol Action |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Low** | Unusual CPU/Resource spike | Log + notify user via the Acolyte |
| **Medium** | Attempted cross-module access | Immediate termination of the module |
| **High** | Signature/Attestation failure | Permanent quarantine + Security Alert |

---

## 🛡️ The Sovereignty Guarantee
1. **Ephemeral Biometrics:** No module is allowed to store biometric data permanently. Data must exist only in volatile memory during the computation of the clinical result.
2. **Audit Trails:** The protocol maintains a local, user-inspectable log of every time a module requested access to a hardware sensor.
3. **Hardware Kill-Switch:** The user can revoke a module's access to any specific sensor (Microphone, Camera, Heart Rate) at the protocol level, bypassing the module's own logic.

---

## 🛠️ Implementation Stack (Universal)

| Layer | Implementation Strategy |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Process Isolation** | Namespaces / Cgroups (Linux) / AppContainer (Windows) |
| **Communication** | Secure Message Bus (gRPC / Unix Sockets / Binder) |
| **Encryption** | AES-256 for all local inter-module traffic |
| **Enforcement** | Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL) Core |

---
> *"Isolation is the technical wall that protects human dignity. If the code is not isolated, the user is not sovereign."*

```

B5. USER-DATA-MODEL.md

```markdown
# 📊 User Data Model: Sovereign Mathematical Tensors

### The Standard for Ephemeral and Private Physiological Information
This document defines how the **Cortex Protocol** structures and protects user data. Following the **Mathematical Privacy Layer**, this model ensures that raw physiological signals are never stored; only anonymized, sovereign tensors exist within the system.
---

## 🧭 Design Philosophy: Data as a Biological Extension

User data in the Cortex Protocol follows three absolute principles:
1. **Ephemeral by Default:** Raw biometric signals (HRV, EEG, Voice) exist only in volatile memory (RAM) and are destroyed immediately after being processed into mathematical tensors.
2. **Sovereign Encryption:** Any data that persists (user preferences, local learning weights) is encrypted using hardware-backed keys (Secure Enclave) that the Protocol cannot access without a direct user command.
3. **Information over Data:** We store the *meaning* (e.g., "State: Flow") rather than the *measurement* (e.g., "Heart Rate: 85bpm").
---

## 📐 Data Layers
The protocol organizes information into three distinct, isolated layers:

### 1. The Transient Layer (Raw Signals)
- **Status:** **NON-PERSISTENT.**
- **Content:** Raw buffers from microphones, heart rate sensors, and environmental sensors.
- **Handling:** These stay within the **Sovereignty Abstraction Layer (SAL)**. They are piped directly into the Mathematical Privacy Layer and then wiped from memory.

### 2. The Tensor Layer (Anonymized Features)
- **Status:** **EPHEMERAL / ENCRYPTED.**
- **Content:** Vectorized mathematical representations of the user's state. 
- **Purpose:** Used by the **Acolyte** to understand intent and cognitive load without knowing the raw biological values.
- **Privacy:** These tensors are processed using **Differential Privacy** to ensure no raw signal can be reconstructed.

### 3. The Insight Layer (Sovereign History)
- **Status:** **OPT-IN / PERSISTENT.**
- **Content:** Derived clinical metrics (e.g., "Weekly Focus Trend", "Ventral Vagal Baseline").
- **Storage:** Stored locally in an encrypted vault.
- **Interoperability:** Uses a simplified version of the **BIDS-Physio** standard, allowing the user to export their history for professional clinical review without compromising their identity.
---

## 🔐 The "No-Trace" Guarantee

| Data Type | Storage Location | Retention | Access Level |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Raw Voice** | RAM only | Milliseconds | SAL only |
| **Raw HRV** | RAM only | Milliseconds | SAL only |
| **State Tensors** | Secure Sandbox | Session only | Acolyte |
| **Clinical Trends** | Encrypted Vault | User-defined | User Only |

---

## 🛠️ Implementation for Contributors
### 🔢 Tensor Conversion (The OpenMined Path)
All modules must emit data in **Encapsulated Tensor** format. A module cannot send a raw integer representing "Heart Rate". It must send a normalized, differentially private vector that the Acolyte's neural engine can interpret.

### 🔑 Key Management
The protocol utilizes the device's **Root of Trust**:
- **Android:** Keystore + OP-TEE.
- **Linux/Desktop:** TPM 2.0 / LUKS.
- **Keys:** Generated locally, never backed up to the cloud, and destroyed if the user invokes the "Protocol Wipe" command.
---

## 📊 Research Interoperability
To support the **Clinical Bridge**, the protocol allows for "Sovereign Research Contributions":
- Users can choose to share **Mathematical Gradients** (not data) with **Governance Nodes** (Universities).
- This uses **Federated Learning**, allowing the protocol to become smarter for everyone while the user's individual data remains on their own silicon.
---
> *"In the Cortex Protocol, your data is not an asset to be harvested. It is a biological signature that belongs only to you. We don't store your life; we help you navigate it."*

```
